data-ccp-charstyle="Emphasis">&nbsp;a Jupyter Notebook ninja in Microsoft Sentinel</SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun  SCXW109037511 BCX8" data-ccp-charstyle="Emphasis">.&nbsp;</SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun  SCXW109037511 BCX8" data-ccp-charstyle="Emphasis">The installments will be bite-sized to enable you to easily digest the new content.</SPAN></SPAN></EM><SPAN class="EOP SCXW109037511 BCX8" data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}">&nbsp;</SPAN></P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<UL>
<LI><STRONG>Part 1:</STRONG> <A href="https://techcommunity.microsoft.com/t5/microsoft-sentinel-blog/becoming-a-microsoft-sentinel-notebooks-ninja-the-series/ba-p/2693491" target="_self">What are notebooks and when do you need them?</A></LI>
<LI><STRONG>Part 2:</STRONG> <A href="https://techcommunity.microsoft.com/t5/azure-sentinel/azure-sentinel-notebooks-ninja-part-2-getting-started-with-azure/ba-p/2716661" target="_self">How to get started with notebooks and tour of the features</A></LI>
<LI><STRONG>Part 3:</STRONG> <A href="https://techcommunity.microsoft.com/t5/microsoft-sentinel-blog/microsoft-sentinel-notebooks-ninja-part-3-overview-of-the-pre/ba-p/2768838" target="_blank">Overview of the pre-built notebooks and how to use them</A></LI>
<LI><STRONG>Part 3.5:</STRONG>&nbsp;<A href="https://techcommunity.microsoft.com/t5/microsoft-sentinel-blog/using-code-snippets-to-build-your-own-sentinel-notebooks/ba-p/2965208" target="_self">Using Code Snippets to build your own Sentinel Notebooks</A>&nbsp;</LI>
<LI><STRONG>Part 4:</STRONG> <A href="https://techcommunity.microsoft.com/t5/microsoft-sentinel-blog/creating-your-first-microsoft-sentinel-notebook/ba-p/2977745" target="_blank">How to create your own notebooks from scratch and how to customize the existing ones</A> – <STRONG><EM>this post</EM></STRONG></LI>
</UL>
<P><STRONG>KNOWLEDGE CHECK:</STRONG>&nbsp;And, once you've completed all of the parts of this series, you can take the <A href="https://aka.ms/SentinelNotebookQuiz" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">Knowledge Check</A>.&nbsp;If you score 80% or more in the <A href="https://aka.ms/SentinelNotebookQuiz" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">Knowledge Check</A>, you can expect your very own Notebooks Ninja participation certificate from us.</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P><SPAN data-contrast="auto">Jupyter&nbsp;Notebooks are a fantastic resource for security analysts,&nbsp;providing&nbsp;a range of powerful and flexible capabilities.&nbsp;Microsoft Sentinel’s integration with&nbsp;Notebooks&nbsp;can&nbsp;provide&nbsp;a quick and&nbsp;straightforward way&nbsp;for security analysts to use&nbsp;Notebooks, however for those new to&nbsp;Notebooks and coding they can be a little daunting.</SPAN><SPAN data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}">&nbsp;</SPAN></P>
<P><SPAN data-contrast="auto">In&nbsp;this blog we will cover some of the basics&nbsp;of creating your first Microsoft Sentinel&nbsp;Notebook&nbsp;using Python, including how to troubleshoot some common issues you may come across.&nbsp;</SPAN><SPAN data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}">&nbsp;</SPAN></P>
<UL>
<LI data-leveltext="" data-font="Symbol" data-listid="8" aria-setsize="-1" data-aria-posinset="1" data-aria-level="1"><SPAN data-contrast="auto">Installing and importing packages in Python</SPAN><SPAN data-ccp-props="{&quot;134233279&quot;:true,&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}">&nbsp;</SPAN></LI>
<LI data-leveltext="" data-font="Symbol" data-listid="8" aria-setsize="-1" data-aria-posinset="2" data-aria-level="1"><SPAN data-contrast="auto">Installing and importing&nbsp;MSTICPy</SPAN><SPAN data-ccp-props="{&quot;134233279&quot;:true,&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}">&nbsp;</SPAN></LI>
<LI data-leveltext="" data-font="Symbol" data-listid="8" aria-setsize="-1" data-aria-posinset="3" data-aria-level="1"><SPAN data-contrast="auto">Setting up&nbsp;MSTICPy’s&nbsp;config file</SPAN><SPAN data-ccp-props="{&quot;134233279&quot;:true,&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}">&nbsp;</SPAN></LI>
<LI data-leveltext="" data-font="Symbol" data-listid="8" aria-setsize="-1" data-aria-posinset="4" data-aria-level="1"><SPAN data-contrast="auto">Getting data from Microsoft Sentinel</SPAN><SPAN data-ccp-props="{&quot;134233279&quot;:true,&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}">&nbsp;</SPAN></LI>
<LI data-leveltext="" data-font="Symbol" data-listid="8" aria-setsize="-1" data-aria-posinset="5" data-aria-level="1"><SPAN data-contrast="auto">Working with data</SPAN><SPAN data-ccp-props="{&quot;134233279&quot;:true,&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}">&nbsp;</SPAN></LI>
<LI data-leveltext="" data-font="Symbol" data-listid="8" aria-setsize="-1" data-aria-posinset="6" data-aria-level="1"><SPAN data-contrast="auto">Enriching&nbsp;results&nbsp;with external data sources</SPAN><SPAN data-ccp-props="{&quot;134233279&quot;:true,&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}">&nbsp;</SPAN></LI>
<LI data-leveltext="" data-font="Symbol" data-listid="8" aria-setsize="-1" data-aria-posinset="7" data-aria-level="1"><SPAN data-contrast="auto">Visualizations with&nbsp;MSTICPy</SPAN><SPAN data-ccp-props="{&quot;134233279&quot;:true,&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}">&nbsp;</SPAN></LI>
</UL>
<P><SPAN data-contrast="auto">Before we begin,&nbsp;make sure to familiarize yourself with&nbsp;Notebooks in Microsoft Sentinel via Azure Machine Learning.&nbsp;</SPAN><SPAN data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}">&nbsp;</SPAN></P>
<P><A href="https://docs.microsoft.com/en-us/azure/sentinel/notebooks" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer"><SPAN data-contrast="none">Use Jupyter&nbsp;Notebooks to hunt for security threats&nbsp;</SPAN></A><SPAN data-contrast="auto">&nbsp;</SPAN><SPAN data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559731&quot;:720,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}">&nbsp;</SPAN></P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P><SPAN data-contrast="auto">If you wish to learn more about this&nbsp;topic,&nbsp;we are running&nbsp;introductory training on December 16th,&nbsp;2021: Become a&nbsp;Jupyter&nbsp;Notebooks Ninja –&nbsp;MSTICPy&nbsp;Fundamentals to Build Your Own&nbsp;Notebooks</SPAN><SPAN data-contrast="auto">.</SPAN><SPAN data-contrast="auto">&nbsp;</SPAN><A href="https://forms.office.com/pages/responsepage.aspx?id=v4j5cvGGr0GRqy180BHbR2HneBfpDd1Mj3-yGKE5Q-xUNkVRQkNPTlFXSzVFRzZFSURFWkRKM0hWUi4u" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer"><SPAN data-contrast="none">Sign Up Here</SPAN></A><SPAN data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}">&nbsp;</SPAN></P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<H2 aria-level="2" id="community-2977745-toc-hId--293249455"><SPAN data-contrast="none">Installing and Importing Packages in Python</SPAN><SPAN data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559738&quot;:40,&quot;335559739&quot;:0,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}">&nbsp;</SPAN></H2>
<P><SPAN data-contrast="auto">One of the&nbsp;important things&nbsp;about using Python in&nbsp;Notebooks is that you can install and use code libraries (referred to as packages) created by others, allowing you to access the functionality they provide without having to code them yourself.</SPAN><SPAN data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}">&nbsp;</SPAN></P>
<P><SPAN data-contrast="auto">There are several ways to install&nbsp;Python packages&nbsp;depending on how you want to&nbsp;find and&nbsp;access the&nbsp;packages, however the simplest and easiest is using pip. Pip&nbsp;(<A href="https://pypi.org/project/pip/" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow noreferrer">https://pypi.org/project/pip/</A>) is the&nbsp;package&nbsp;installer for Python and makes finding and installing Python&nbsp;packages&nbsp;simple.</SPAN><SPAN data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}">&nbsp;</SPAN></P>
<P><SPAN data-contrast="auto">You can use pip to install packages via the command line, or if you are using a&nbsp;Notebook, directly in a&nbsp;Notebook&nbsp;cell.&nbsp;Installing directly in a&nbsp;Notebook&nbsp;is often preferred as it ensures that you are installing the package in the same Python environment the&nbsp;Notebook&nbsp;is being executed in.&nbsp;To&nbsp;install via a&nbsp;Notebook&nbsp;code&nbsp;cell,&nbsp;we&nbsp;need to use `%pip` followed by install and the&nbsp;package&nbsp;name. e.g.:</SPAN><SPAN data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}">&nbsp;</SPAN></P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<pre class="lia-code-sample language-python"><code>%pip install requests</code></pre>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P><span class="lia-media-object lia-media-is-center lia-media-size-large" data-image-alt="PeteBryan_0-1637179707416.png"><button class="lia-media-unstyled-btn" type="button" aria-haspopup="true" aria-label="Enlarge Image PeteBryan_0-1637179707416.png"><img src="https://techcommunity.microsoft.com/t5/s/gxcuf89792/images/bS0yOTc3NzQ1LTMyNzc1NmkwRjAxRUMyRkYwOEVGMEFF?image-dimensions=999x235&amp;revision=14" width="999" height="235" alt="PeteBryan_0-1637179707416.png" /></button><span class="lia-media-caption-text">Notebook output of running %pip install requests</span></span></P>
<P style="border: solid 1px; padding: 10px; background-color: #fafaff;"><STRONG>Note: </STRONG> `%pip` is what is called a magic function in Jupyter. This tells the Notebook to use pip to install the package in the Notebooks compute environment.</P>
<P><SPAN class="TextRun SCXW210062414 BCX8" data-contrast="auto"><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW210062414 BCX8">If you already have a package installed but you want to update to the latest<SPAN>&nbsp;</SPAN></SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW210062414 BCX8">version,</SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW210062414 BCX8"><SPAN>&nbsp;</SPAN>you can add the `--upgrade` parameter to the command used:</SPAN></SPAN><SPAN class="EOP SCXW210062414 BCX8" data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}">&nbsp;</SPAN></P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<pre class="lia-code-sample language-python"><code>%pip install –upgrade requests</code></pre>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P><SPAN class="EOP SCXW210062414 BCX8" data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}"><SPAN class="TextRun SCXW260976833 BCX8" data-contrast="auto"><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW260976833 BCX8">You may also want to install a specific version of a package. This can be done by specifying the version number.</SPAN></SPAN><SPAN class="EOP SCXW260976833 BCX8" data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}">&nbsp;</SPAN></SPAN></P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<pre class="lia-code-sample language-python"><code>%pip install requests==2.22.0</code></pre>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P><span class="lia-media-object lia-media-is-inline lia-media-size-large" data-image-alt="PeteBryan_1-163717993upgrading a package.0921.png"><button class="lia-media-unstyled-btn" type="button" aria-haspopup="true" aria-label="Enlarge Image PeteBryan_1-163717993upgrading a package.0921.png"><img src="https://techcommunity.microsoft.com/t5/s/gxcuf89792/images/bS0yOTc3NzQ1LTMyNzc1OGkyRkVDOEIxNEI5QTFFQTUy?image-dimensions=999x182&amp;revision=14" width="999" height="182" alt="PeteBryan_1-163717993upgrading a package.0921.png" /></button><span class="lia-media-caption-text">Output of running %pip install requests==2.22.0</span></span></P>
<P style="border: solid 1px; padding: 10px; background-color: #fafaff;"><STRONG>Note: </STRONG> &nbsp;Once you have installed a package&nbsp;it is&nbsp;recommended&nbsp;to restart the&nbsp;Notebook&nbsp;kernel, this will ensure that when you import the package you will be using the latest version. This&nbsp;is not&nbsp;necessary with newly installed packages but is important when</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P style="border: solid 1px; padding: 10px; background-color: #fafaff;"><STRONG>Note: </STRONG> &nbsp;During installation of packages you may see some warnings related to package dependencies. This is because some packages have requirements on other packages being installed and sometimes these requirements can have conflicts (i.e., package 1 requires package A version 1.1 but package 2 also requires package A but version 1.2). We try to avoid conflicts as much as possible with our Notebooks but sometimes these can occur. You can usually run the Notebook without the conflicts affecting you. However, if you encounter a problem with a pre-made Microsoft Sentinel Notebook, please report this at via <A href="https://github.com/Azure/Azure-Sentinel-Notebooks/issues" target="_self" rel="noopener noreferrer">GitHub</A>.</P>
<P><SPAN data-contrast="auto">Once a package is installed,&nbsp;you&nbsp;need&nbsp;to&nbsp;import&nbsp;the package&nbsp;before it can be used. This is done with the `import` statement.</SPAN><SPAN data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}">&nbsp;</SPAN></P>
<P><SPAN data-contrast="auto">There&nbsp;are 2 ways to import things in Python:</SPAN><SPAN data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}">&nbsp;</SPAN></P>
<P><SPAN data-contrast="auto">- `import &lt;package&gt;` -&nbsp;this&nbsp;will&nbsp;do a standard import of the&nbsp;package</SPAN><SPAN data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}">&nbsp;</SPAN></P>
<P><SPAN data-contrast="auto">- `from &lt;package&gt; import &lt;item&gt;` - this imports a specific item from the package</SPAN><SPAN data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}">&nbsp;</SPAN></P>
<P><SPAN data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}">&nbsp;</SPAN></P>
<P><SPAN data-contrast="auto">You can also import packages and rename them for ease when calling them later:</SPAN><SPAN data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}">&nbsp;</SPAN></P>
<P><SPAN data-contrast="auto">`import &lt;package&gt; as &lt;alias&gt;`</SPAN><SPAN data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}">&nbsp;</SPAN></P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<pre class="lia-code-sample language-python"><code>import pandas as pd</code></pre>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P style="border: solid 1px; padding: 10px; background-color: #fafaff;"><STRONG>Troubleshooting Tip: </STRONG> Some packages do not use the same name for installation and import. You many need to check package documentation to ensure you are importing correctly.</P>
<P><SPAN class="TextRun SCXW230817682 BCX8" data-contrast="auto"><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW230817682 BCX8">For<SPAN>&nbsp;</SPAN></SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW230817682 BCX8">example,</SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW230817682 BCX8"><SPAN>&nbsp;</SPAN>the popular Machine Learning tool package<SPAN>&nbsp;</SPAN></SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW230817682 BCX8">scikit-learn</SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW230817682 BCX8"><SPAN>&nbsp;</SPAN>is installed with:</SPAN></SPAN><SPAN class="EOP SCXW230817682 BCX8" data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}">&nbsp;</SPAN></P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<pre class="lia-code-sample language-python"><code>%pip install scikit-learn</code></pre>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P><SPAN class="TextRun SCXW187946870 BCX8" data-contrast="auto"><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW187946870 BCX8">However, it is imported with:</SPAN></SPAN><SPAN class="EOP SCXW187946870 BCX8" data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}">&nbsp;</SPAN></P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<pre class="lia-code-sample language-python"><code>import sklearn</code></pre>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<H2 aria-level="2" id="community-2977745-toc-hId--2100703918"><SPAN data-contrast="none">Installing and Importing&nbsp;MSTICPy</SPAN><SPAN data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559738&quot;:40,&quot;335559739&quot;:0,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}">&nbsp;</SPAN></H2>
<P><SPAN data-contrast="auto">Now that&nbsp;we know how to install and import&nbsp;packages,&nbsp;we can install packages that will be useful to us in creating our&nbsp;Notebook.&nbsp;MSTICPy&nbsp;is a package created by the Microsoft Threat Intelligence Center (MSTIC) and provides a range of tools to make security analysis and investigations in&nbsp;Notebooks quicker and easier. You cand find out more about&nbsp;MSTICPy&nbsp;here:</SPAN><SPAN data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}">&nbsp;</SPAN></P>
<P><A href="https://msticpy.readthedocs.io/en/latest/GettingStarted.html" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow noreferrer"><SPAN data-contrast="none">ReadTheDocs - MSTICPy</SPAN></A><SPAN data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}">&nbsp;</SPAN></P>
<P><SPAN data-contrast="auto">We can now install&nbsp;MSTICPy. To make sure we get the latest version if we already have it&nbsp;installed,&nbsp;we are going to use the –upgrade parameter.</SPAN><SPAN data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}">&nbsp;</SPAN></P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<pre class="lia-code-sample language-python"><code>%pip install --upgrade msticpy </code></pre>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P><SPAN class="TextRun SCXW144367884 BCX8" data-contrast="auto"><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW144367884 BCX8">Now we could import<SPAN>&nbsp;</SPAN></SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SpellingErrorV2 SCXW144367884 BCX8">MSTICPy</SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW144367884 BCX8"><SPAN>&nbsp;</SPAN></SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW144367884 BCX8">with</SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW144367884 BCX8"><SPAN>&nbsp;</SPAN>`import<SPAN>&nbsp;</SPAN></SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SpellingErrorV2 SCXW144367884 BCX8">msticpy</SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW144367884 BCX8">` however<SPAN>&nbsp;</SPAN></SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW144367884 BCX8">it is</SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW144367884 BCX8"><SPAN>&nbsp;</SPAN>a big<SPAN>&nbsp;</SPAN></SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW144367884 BCX8">package</SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW144367884 BCX8"><SPAN>&nbsp;</SPAN>with a lot of features, so to make it easier<SPAN>&nbsp;</SPAN></SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW144367884 BCX8">we have a function called `</SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SpellingErrorV2 SCXW144367884 BCX8">init_notebook</SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW144367884 BCX8">` that conducts<SPAN>&nbsp;</SPAN></SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW144367884 BCX8">several</SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW144367884 BCX8"><SPAN>&nbsp;</SPAN>checks to make sure the environment is good, handles key imports and set up for us.</SPAN></SPAN><SPAN class="EOP SCXW144367884 BCX8" data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:2,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:255}">&nbsp;</SPAN></P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<pre class="lia-code-sample language-python"><code>import msticpy
msticpy.init_notebook(globals())</code></pre>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P><span class="lia-media-object lia-media-is-inline lia-media-size-large" data-image-alt="PeteBryan_2-1637180256693.png"><button class="lia-media-unstyled-btn" type="button" aria-haspopup="true" aria-label="Enlarge Image PeteBryan_2-1637180256693.png"><img src="https://techcommunity.microsoft.com/t5/s/gxcuf89792/images/bS0yOTc3NzQ1LTMyNzc1OWk2Mzk4NzNGNEVDMkIzNDUx?image-dimensions=999x574&amp;revision=14" width="999" height="574" alt="PeteBryan_2-1637180256693.png" /></button><span class="lia-media-caption-text">Notebook output of running previous code cell.</span></span></P>
<H2 aria-level="2" id="community-2977745-toc-hId-386808915"><SPAN data-contrast="none">Setting up&nbsp;MSTICPy’s&nbsp;Config File</SPAN><SPAN data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559738&quot;:40,&quot;335559739&quot;:0,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}">&nbsp;</SPAN></H2>
<P><SPAN data-contrast="auto">MSTICPy&nbsp;can handle connections to a variety of data sources and services, including Microsoft Sentinel. As such it needs&nbsp;to handle&nbsp;several&nbsp;configuration details and credentials, things such as the Microsoft Sentinel workspaces you want to get data from, or&nbsp;API (Application Programming Interfaces)&nbsp;keys for external services such as&nbsp;Virus Total.</SPAN><SPAN data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}">&nbsp;</SPAN></P>
<P><SPAN data-contrast="auto">To make it easier to manage and re-use the configuration and credentials for these things&nbsp;MSTICPy&nbsp;has its own config file that holds these items - `msticpyconfig.yaml`.</SPAN><SPAN data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}">&nbsp;</SPAN></P>
<P><SPAN data-contrast="auto">The first time you use&nbsp;MSTICPy&nbsp;you need to populate your&nbsp;msticpyconfig.yaml&nbsp;file. This is a&nbsp;one-time&nbsp;activity&nbsp;once&nbsp;you have created it,&nbsp;you can simply re-use&nbsp;in future. To help with the&nbsp;set-up&nbsp;we have created&nbsp;several&nbsp;Notebook&nbsp;widgets to help you populate the file.</SPAN><SPAN data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}">&nbsp;</SPAN></P>
<P><span class="lia-media-object lia-media-is-inline lia-media-size-large" data-image-alt="PeteBryan_3-1637180304684.png"><button class="lia-media-unstyled-btn" type="button" aria-haspopup="true" aria-label="Enlarge Image PeteBryan_3-1637180304684.png"><img src="https://techcommunity.microsoft.com/t5/s/gxcuf89792/images/bS0yOTc3NzQ1LTMyNzc2MGk1QjlDMTJGRDI1QTcyN0I5?image-dimensions=926x412&amp;revision=14" width="926" height="412" alt="PeteBryan_3-1637180304684.png" /></button></span></P>
<P style="border: solid 1px; padding: 10px; background-color: #fafaff;"><STRONG>Note: </STRONG>If using Azure Machine Learning then you may notice this config widget can take some time to load. We are working to improve this but if you run the notebook in Jupyter, JupyterLab or VSCode you will not have these performance issues.</P>
<P><SPAN class="TextRun SCXW111946729 BCX8" data-contrast="auto"><SPAN class="NormalTextRun CommentStart SCXW111946729 BCX8">We have also created a<SPAN>&nbsp;</SPAN></SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW111946729 BCX8">Notebook</SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW111946729 BCX8"><SPAN>&nbsp;</SPAN>to help you create to file</SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW111946729 BCX8">. Once<SPAN>&nbsp;</SPAN></SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW111946729 BCX8">you have run the<SPAN>&nbsp;</SPAN></SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW111946729 BCX8">‘</SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW111946729 BCX8">Getting Started</SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW111946729 BCX8">’</SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW111946729 BCX8">&nbsp;</SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW111946729 BCX8">N</SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW111946729 BCX8">otebook&nbsp;</SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW111946729 BCX8">it is<SPAN>&nbsp;</SPAN></SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW111946729 BCX8">recommended</SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW111946729 BCX8"><SPAN>&nbsp;</SPAN>that you run<SPAN>&nbsp;</SPAN></SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW111946729 BCX8">the<SPAN>&nbsp;</SPAN></SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW111946729 BCX8">‘</SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW111946729 BCX8">Configuring your Notebook Environmen</SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW111946729 BCX8">t</SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW111946729 BCX8">’</SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW111946729 BCX8"><SPAN>&nbsp;</SPAN>Notebook</SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW111946729 BCX8"><SPAN>&nbsp;</SPAN>before creating your first<SPAN>&nbsp;</SPAN></SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW111946729 BCX8">Notebook</SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW111946729 BCX8">, you can find this in the Microsoft Sentinel portal.</SPAN></SPAN></P>
<P><SPAN class="EOP SCXW111946729 BCX8" data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}">&nbsp;</SPAN></P>
<P><span class="lia-media-object lia-media-is-inline lia-media-size-large" data-image-alt="PeteBryan_4-1637180355578.png"><button class="lia-media-unstyled-btn" type="button" aria-haspopup="true" aria-label="Enlarge Image PeteBryan_4-1637180355578.png"><img src="https://techcommunity.microsoft.com/t5/s/gxcuf89792/images/bS0yOTc3NzQ1LTMyNzc2MWk1RDk5MTA2QUVBQUM4NjBC?image-dimensions=999x732&amp;revision=14" width="999" height="732" alt="PeteBryan_4-1637180355578.png" /></button><span class="lia-media-caption-text">Microsoft Sentinel Notebook feature blade highlighting the Configuring you Notebook Environment Notebook</span></span></P>
<P><SPAN class="TextRun SCXW35822288 BCX8" data-contrast="auto"><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW35822288 BCX8">&nbsp;You can also find more documentation on the config file and creati</SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW35822288 BCX8">on of</SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW35822288 BCX8">&nbsp;</SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW35822288 BCX8">it</SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW35822288 BCX8">,</SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW35822288 BCX8">&nbsp;</SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW35822288 BCX8">in the<SPAN>&nbsp;</SPAN></SPAN></SPAN><A class="Hyperlink SCXW35822288 BCX8" href="https://msticpy.readthedocs.io/en/latest/getting_started/SettingsEditor.html" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener nofollow"><SPAN class="TextRun Underlined SCXW35822288 BCX8" data-contrast="none"><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW35822288 BCX8" data-ccp-charstyle="Hyperlink">MSTICPy</SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW35822288 BCX8" data-ccp-charstyle="Hyperlink"><SPAN>&nbsp;</SPAN>docs</SPAN></SPAN></A><SPAN class="TextRun SCXW35822288 BCX8" data-contrast="auto"><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW35822288 BCX8"><SPAN>&nbsp;</SPAN></SPAN></SPAN><SPAN class="EOP SCXW35822288 BCX8" data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}">&nbsp;</SPAN></P>
<P aria-level="2">&nbsp;</P>
<H2 aria-level="2" id="community-2977745-toc-hId--1420645548"><SPAN data-contrast="none">Getting Data from Microsoft Sentinel&nbsp;</SPAN><SPAN data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559738&quot;:40,&quot;335559739&quot;:0,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}">&nbsp;</SPAN></H2>
<P><SPAN data-contrast="auto">Querying data from&nbsp;Microsoft Sentinel&nbsp;is handled by&nbsp;MSTICPy's&nbsp;`QueryProvider`. The first step is to initialize a&nbsp;QueryProvider&nbsp;and tell it we want to use the&nbsp;Microsoft&nbsp;Sentinel Query provider.</SPAN><SPAN data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}">&nbsp;</SPAN></P>
<P style="border: solid 1px; padding: 10px; background-color: #fafaff;"><STRONG>Note: </STRONG>MSTICPy contains several QueryProviders for other data sources as well.</P>
<P><SPAN class="TextRun SCXW124740381 BCX8" data-contrast="auto"><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW124740381 BCX8">The other thing we want to provide the<SPAN>&nbsp;</SPAN></SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SpellingErrorV2 SCXW124740381 BCX8">QueryProvider</SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW124740381 BCX8"><SPAN>&nbsp;</SPAN>with is some details of the workspace we want to connect to. We *could* do this manually, but<SPAN>&nbsp;</SPAN></SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW124740381 BCX8">it is</SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW124740381 BCX8"><SPAN>&nbsp;</SPAN>much easier to get details from the configuration we set up earlier. We can do this with `</SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SpellingErrorV2 SCXW124740381 BCX8">WorkspaceConfig</SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW124740381 BCX8">`</SPAN></SPAN><SPAN class="EOP SCXW124740381 BCX8" data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}">&nbsp;</SPAN></P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<pre class="lia-code-sample language-python"><code>from msticpy.nbtools import nbinit
nbinit.init_Notebook(namespace=globals())
qry_prov=QueryProvider("MicrosoftSentinel")
ws_config = WorkspaceConfig(workspace="MyWorkspace") </code></pre>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P><SPAN class="TextRun SCXW29079112 BCX8" data-contrast="auto"><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW29079112 BCX8">What<SPAN>&nbsp;</SPAN></SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SpellingErrorV2 SCXW29079112 BCX8 SpellingErrorHighlight">WorkspaceConfig</SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW29079112 BCX8"><SPAN>&nbsp;</SPAN>is<SPAN>&nbsp;</SPAN></SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW29079112 BCX8">doing</SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW29079112 BCX8"><SPAN>&nbsp;</SPAN>is creating the connection string used by the<SPAN>&nbsp;</SPAN></SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SpellingErrorV2 SCXW29079112 BCX8">QueryProvider</SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW29079112 BCX8">. We can see what that connection string looks like with:</SPAN></SPAN><SPAN class="EOP SCXW29079112 BCX8" data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}">&nbsp;</SPAN></P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<pre class="lia-code-sample language-python"><code>ws_config.code_connect_str </code></pre>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P><span class="lia-media-object lia-media-is-inline lia-media-size-large" data-image-alt="PeteBryan_5-1637180517161.png"><button class="lia-media-unstyled-btn" type="button" aria-haspopup="true" aria-label="Enlarge Image PeteBryan_5-1637180517161.png"><img src="https://techcommunity.microsoft.com/t5/s/gxcuf89792/images/bS0yOTc3NzQ1LTMyNzc2M2k5QzE4REM0QUU4NzQ5QTY0?image-dimensions=999x113&amp;revision=14" width="999" height="113" alt="PeteBryan_5-1637180517161.png" /></button><span class="lia-media-caption-text">Notebook output showing the connection string generated by code_connect_str</span></span></P>
<P><SPAN class="EOP SCXW29079112 BCX8" data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}"><SPAN class="TextRun SCXW54064775 BCX8" data-contrast="auto"><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW54064775 BCX8">Once set up we can tell the `</SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SpellingErrorV2 SCXW54064775 BCX8">QueryProvider</SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW54064775 BCX8">` to `connect` which will kick off the authentication process. There are<SPAN>&nbsp;</SPAN></SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW54064775 BCX8">several</SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW54064775 BCX8"><SPAN>&nbsp;</SPAN>ways that we can handle that authentication but when starting off we can use the default options that prompts the user to log in using a<SPAN>&nbsp;</SPAN></SPAN></SPAN><A class="Hyperlink SCXW54064775 BCX8" href="https://docs.microsoft.com/en-us/azure/active-directory/develop/msal-authentication-flows#device-code" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener"><SPAN class="TextRun SCXW54064775 BCX8" data-contrast="auto"><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW54064775 BCX8">Device Code</SPAN></SPAN></A><SPAN class="TextRun SCXW54064775 BCX8" data-contrast="auto"><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW54064775 BCX8">.</SPAN></SPAN><SPAN class="EOP SCXW54064775 BCX8" data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}">&nbsp;</SPAN></SPAN></P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<pre class="lia-code-sample language-python"><code>qry_prov.connect(ws_config) </code></pre>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P><SPAN class="EOP SCXW29079112 BCX8" data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}"><SPAN class="EOP SCXW54064775 BCX8" data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}"><SPAN class="TextRun SCXW83964423 BCX8" data-contrast="auto"><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW83964423 BCX8">This will then display a code in the<SPAN>&nbsp;</SPAN></SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW83964423 BCX8">Notebook</SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW83964423 BCX8"><SPAN>&nbsp;</SPAN>cell output and prompt you to open a browser and end the code shown. You will then login as normal<SPAN>&nbsp;</SPAN></SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW83964423 BCX8">using your Azure<SPAN>&nbsp;</SPAN></SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW83964423 BCX8">AD (Azure Active Directory)</SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW83964423 BCX8"><SPAN>&nbsp;</SPAN>credentials.&nbsp;</SPAN></SPAN><SPAN class="EOP SCXW83964423 BCX8" data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}">&nbsp;</SPAN></SPAN></SPAN></P>
<P><span class="lia-media-object lia-media-is-center lia-media-size-large" data-image-alt="PeteBryan_6-1637180682556.png"><button class="lia-media-unstyled-btn" type="button" aria-haspopup="true" aria-label="Enlarge Image PeteBryan_6-1637180682556.png"><img src="https://techcommunity.microsoft.com/t5/s/gxcuf89792/images/bS0yOTc3NzQ1LTMyNzc2NGlDQkIxODQyQTY2NENFMTc4?image-dimensions=999x264&amp;revision=14" width="999" height="264" alt="PeteBryan_6-1637180682556.png" /></button><span class="lia-media-caption-text">Screenshots of the Device Code authentication flow</span></span></P>
<P><SPAN class="TextRun SCXW75116665 BCX8" data-contrast="auto"><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW75116665 BCX8">&nbsp;</SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW75116665 BCX8">You can then go back to the<SPAN>&nbsp;</SPAN></SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW75116665 BCX8">Notebook</SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW75116665 BCX8"><SPAN>&nbsp;</SPAN>and see that the authentication has<SPAN>&nbsp;</SPAN></SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW75116665 BCX8">been completed</SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW75116665 BCX8">:</SPAN></SPAN><SPAN class="EOP SCXW75116665 BCX8" data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}">&nbsp;</SPAN></P>
<P><span class="lia-media-object lia-media-is-center lia-media-size-large" data-image-alt="PeteBryan_7-1637180719500.png"><button class="lia-media-unstyled-btn" type="button" aria-haspopup="true" aria-label="Enlarge Image PeteBryan_7-1637180719500.png"><img src="https://techcommunity.microsoft.com/t5/s/gxcuf89792/images/bS0yOTc3NzQ1LTMyNzc2NWk1Mjk3NjQ0QjE5NEUzNjg0?image-dimensions=999x393&amp;revision=14" width="999" height="393" alt="PeteBryan_7-1637180719500.png" /></button><span class="lia-media-caption-text">Notebook output showing the completed authentication flow</span></span></P>
<H3 aria-level="3" id="community-2977745-toc-hId--730084074"><SPAN data-contrast="none">Built-in Queries</SPAN><SPAN data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559738&quot;:40,&quot;335559739&quot;:0,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}">&nbsp;</SPAN></H3>
<P><SPAN data-contrast="auto">Now that we are connected to Microsoft&nbsp;Sentinel,&nbsp;we can start to look at running some queries to get some data.&nbsp;MSTICPy&nbsp;comes with&nbsp;several&nbsp;built-in&nbsp;Microsoft&nbsp;Sentinel queries to get some common datasets into the&nbsp;Notebook. These are different to the queries included in the Microsoft Sentinel GitHub and are more focused on collecting common sets of data that users might&nbsp;need&nbsp;to answer analytical questions.</SPAN><SPAN data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}">&nbsp;</SPAN></P>
<P><SPAN data-contrast="auto">You can see a list of the&nbsp;MSTICPy&nbsp;queries with&nbsp;`.list_queries.`</SPAN><SPAN data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}">&nbsp;</SPAN></P>
<P><span class="lia-media-object lia-media-is-center lia-media-size-large" data-image-alt="PeteBryan_0-1637185073766.png"><button class="lia-media-unstyled-btn" type="button" aria-haspopup="true" aria-label="Enlarge Image PeteBryan_0-1637185073766.png"><img src="https://techcommunity.microsoft.com/t5/s/gxcuf89792/images/bS0yOTc3NzQ1LTMyNzc4MGlGRTg2NjkwNUZBMThGMUE4?image-dimensions=999x653&amp;revision=14" width="999" height="653" alt="PeteBryan_0-1637185073766.png" /></button><span class="lia-media-caption-text">Notebook output of the list_queries command</span></span></P>
<P style="border: solid 1px; padding: 10px; background-color: #fafaff;"><STRONG>Note: </STRONG>MSTICPy also includes queries for its other Data Providers, and not just Microsoft Sentinel.</P>
<P><SPAN class="TextRun SCXW257183314 BCX8" data-contrast="auto"><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW257183314 BCX8">You can also use `.</SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SpellingErrorV2 SCXW257183314 BCX8">browse_queries</SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW257183314 BCX8">()` to see the available queries in an interactive browser widget.</SPAN></SPAN><SPAN class="EOP SCXW257183314 BCX8" data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}">&nbsp;</SPAN></P>
<P><span class="lia-media-object lia-media-is-center lia-media-size-large" data-image-alt="PeteBryan_1-1637185277131.png"><button class="lia-media-unstyled-btn" type="button" aria-haspopup="true" aria-label="Enlarge Image PeteBryan_1-1637185277131.png"><img src="https://techcommunity.microsoft.com/t5/s/gxcuf89792/images/bS0yOTc3NzQ1LTMyNzc4MWk4MzNGRjg2QUM3MUUzMzc5?image-dimensions=999x749&amp;revision=14" width="999" height="749" alt="PeteBryan_1-1637185277131.png" /></button><span class="lia-media-caption-text">Notebook output of browse_queries</span></span></P>
<H3 aria-level="3" id="community-2977745-toc-hId-1757428759"><SPAN data-contrast="none">Running a query</SPAN><SPAN data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559738&quot;:40,&quot;335559739&quot;:0,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}">&nbsp;</SPAN></H3>
<P><SPAN data-contrast="auto">Now that we have found a query that we want to run we simply pass its name to the `QueryProvider` and that in turn returns to results of the query in a&nbsp;</SPAN><A href="https://pandas.pydata.org/" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow noreferrer"><SPAN data-contrast="none">Pandas</SPAN></A><SPAN data-contrast="auto">&nbsp;Data Frame.&nbsp;Most queries&nbsp;support&nbsp;additional&nbsp;parameters,&nbsp;but we are showing one here that does not need any parameters.</SPAN><SPAN data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}">&nbsp;</SPAN></P>
<P style="border: solid 1px; padding: 10px; background-color: #fafaff;"><STRONG>Note: </STRONG>the queries are attached to the QueryProvider as methods (functions) and grouped into categories based on the data source being queried. You can use tab completion or IntelliSense to help you navigate to the query you need.</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<pre class="lia-code-sample language-python"><code>qry_prov.Azure.list_all_signins_geo() </code></pre>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P><span class="lia-media-object lia-media-is-center lia-media-size-large" data-image-alt="PeteBryan_2-1637185753495.png"><button class="lia-media-unstyled-btn" type="button" aria-haspopup="true" aria-label="Enlarge Image PeteBryan_2-1637185753495.png"><img src="https://techcommunity.microsoft.com/t5/s/gxcuf89792/images/bS0yOTc3NzQ1LTMyNzc4Mmk2Q0NCMTMyRDZGQkIzQUQ1?image-dimensions=999x369&amp;revision=14" width="999" height="369" alt="PeteBryan_2-1637185753495.png" /></button><span class="lia-media-caption-text">Output of the list_all_signins_geo query</span></span></P>
<P style="border: solid 1px; padding: 10px; background-color: #fafaff;"><STRONG>Troubleshooting tip: </STRONG>If a query does not execute at first make sure you have run `qry_prov.connect()` to authenticate to Microsoft Sentinel first. Notebook cells do not have to be run in order so you can go back and run any that you missed. However, many notebooks do have cells that rely on previous cells being executed first so be careful about jumping ahead if you have not created the notebook yourself.</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P style="border: solid 1px; padding: 10px; background-color: #fafaff;"><STRONG>Troubleshooting tip: </STRONG>If a query is not returning the results you expect, pass ‘print’ along as a parameter when calling the query to print out the KQL query being executed.</P>
<P><SPAN class="TextRun  BCX8 SCXW110925588" data-contrast="auto"><SPAN class="NormalTextRun  BCX8 SCXW110925588">More typically the query function will expect parameters such as the host name or<SPAN>&nbsp;</SPAN></SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun  BCX8 SCXW110925588">IP</SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun  BCX8 SCXW110925588">&nbsp;address</SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun  BCX8 SCXW110925588"><SPAN>&nbsp;</SPAN>that you are searching for.&nbsp;</SPAN></SPAN><SPAN class="EOP  BCX8 SCXW110925588" data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}">&nbsp;</SPAN></P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<pre class="lia-code-sample language-python"><code>qry_prov.LinuxSyslog.user_logon(host_name="mylxhost") </code></pre>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P><SPAN data-contrast="auto">If you try to run a query without supplying&nbsp;the required&nbsp;parameter, it will return an error message including the help for the query with the parameter definitions.</SPAN><SPAN data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}">&nbsp;</SPAN></P>
<P><SPAN data-contrast="auto">Most queries also require date/time parameters for the beginning/ending bounds of the query. By&nbsp;default,&nbsp;these are supplied by a time&nbsp;range set in the query provider. Each instance of a query provider has its own time range. You can change the default query range&nbsp;by running the following.</SPAN><SPAN data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}">&nbsp;</SPAN></P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<pre class="lia-code-sample language-python"><code>qry_prov.query_time </code></pre>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P><SPAN data-contrast="auto">This brings up a widget letting you change the defaults for this query provider. You can also supply "start” and “end” parameters to the query function – either as Python datetimes or as time strings:</SPAN> <SPAN data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}">&nbsp;</SPAN></P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<pre class="lia-code-sample language-python"><code>from datetime import datetime
qry_prov.LinuxSyslog.user_logon(
    host_name="mylxhost",
    start="2021-11-19 20:30",
    end=datetime.utcnow()
)  </code></pre>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<H2 aria-level="3" id="community-2977745-toc-hId-1746925655"><SPAN data-contrast="none">Customizing Your Queries</SPAN><SPAN data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559738&quot;:40,&quot;335559739&quot;:0,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}">&nbsp;</SPAN></H2>
<P><SPAN data-contrast="auto">In addition to the stock&nbsp;query,&nbsp;we can customize certain elements of the query.</SPAN><SPAN data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}">&nbsp;</SPAN></P>
<P><SPAN data-contrast="auto">For&nbsp;example,&nbsp;if we want to append a&nbsp;line with&nbsp;`| take 10` to the query we have&nbsp;selected&nbsp;to limit the number of results returned we can pass that in with the `add_query_items`&nbsp;parameter:</SPAN><SPAN data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}">&nbsp;</SPAN></P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<pre class="lia-code-sample language-python"><code>qry_prov.SecurityAlert.list_alerts(add_query_items="| take 10") </code></pre>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P><span class="lia-media-object lia-media-is-center lia-media-size-large" data-image-alt="PeteBryan_0-1637201558398.png"><button class="lia-media-unstyled-btn" type="button" aria-haspopup="true" aria-label="Enlarge Image PeteBryan_0-1637201558398.png"><img src="https://techcommunity.microsoft.com/t5/s/gxcuf89792/images/bS0yOTc3NzQ1LTMyNzg0OWlFMjNGMTRCQkM5RTFFNTY1?image-dimensions=999x483&amp;revision=14" width="999" height="483" alt="PeteBryan_0-1637201558398.png" /></button><span class="lia-media-caption-text">The output of the list_alerts query</span></span></P>
<P style="border: solid 1px; padding: 10px; background-color: #fafaff;"><STRONG>Tip: </STRONG>You can also use KQLMagic to query Sentinel data using KQL queries within notebooks. <A href="https://github.com/Microsoft/jupyter-Kqlmagic" target="_self" rel="noopener noreferrer">KQLMagic</A> also returns data in a Pandas Data Frame.</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<H2 aria-level="2" id="community-2977745-toc-hId--60528808"><SPAN data-contrast="none">Working With Data</SPAN><SPAN data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559738&quot;:40,&quot;335559739&quot;:0,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}">&nbsp;</SPAN></H2>
<P><SPAN data-contrast="auto">Data returned by the `QueryProvider` comes back in a Pandas&nbsp;Data Frame. This provides us with a powerful and flexible way to access our data.</SPAN><SPAN data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}">&nbsp;</SPAN></P>
<P><SPAN data-contrast="auto">One of the core things we want to do is look at specific rows in our table. Each table has an index that can be used to call a row using&nbsp;`.loc`, alternatively we can return a row by its position in the table with `.iloc`</SPAN><SPAN data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}">&nbsp;</SPAN></P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<pre class="lia-code-sample language-python"><code>alert_df.loc[1] </code></pre>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P><span class="lia-media-object lia-media-is-center lia-media-size-large" data-image-alt="PeteBryan_1-1637201636603.png"><button class="lia-media-unstyled-btn" type="button" aria-haspopup="true" aria-label="Enlarge Image PeteBryan_1-1637201636603.png"><img src="https://techcommunity.microsoft.com/t5/s/gxcuf89792/images/bS0yOTc3NzQ1LTMyNzg1MGk4MkNCOTZGREVBRDc2MzZE?image-dimensions=999x579&amp;revision=14" width="999" height="579" alt="PeteBryan_1-1637201636603.png" /></button><span class="lia-media-caption-text">Selecting a row with iloc</span></span></P>
<P><SPAN class="TextRun SCXW242056362 BCX8" data-contrast="auto"><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW242056362 BCX8">We can also choose just to return specific columns by<SPAN>&nbsp;</SPAN></SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW242056362 BCX8">providing</SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW242056362 BCX8"><SPAN>&nbsp;</SPAN>a list of them to the<SPAN>&nbsp;</SPAN></SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW242056362 BCX8">Data Frame</SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW242056362 BCX8">&nbsp;(note the "[:5]” means return the last 5 rows)</SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW242056362 BCX8">:</SPAN></SPAN><SPAN class="EOP SCXW242056362 BCX8" data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}">&nbsp;</SPAN></P>
<P><SPAN class="EOP SCXW242056362 BCX8" data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}">&nbsp;</SPAN></P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<pre class="lia-code-sample language-python"><code>alert_df.iloc[:5][["AlertName", "AlertSeverity", "Description"]] </code></pre>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P><span class="lia-media-object lia-media-is-center lia-media-size-large" data-image-alt="PeteBryan_2-1637201671343.png"><button class="lia-media-unstyled-btn" type="button" aria-haspopup="true" aria-label="Enlarge Image PeteBryan_2-1637201671343.png"><img src="https://techcommunity.microsoft.com/t5/s/gxcuf89792/images/bS0yOTc3NzQ1LTMyNzg1MWk1OUQ4MUI5ODg1MDEwOEU2?image-dimensions=999x277&amp;revision=14" width="999" height="277" alt="PeteBryan_2-1637201671343.png" /></button><span class="lia-media-caption-text">Filtering columns of a DataFrame</span></span></P>
<P><SPAN class="TextRun SCXW184641036 BCX8" data-contrast="auto"><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW184641036 BCX8">We can also do things such as search for rows with specific data</SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW184641036 BCX8">:</SPAN></SPAN><SPAN class="EOP SCXW184641036 BCX8" data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}">&nbsp;</SPAN></P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<pre class="lia-code-sample language-python"><code>alert_df[alert_df["AlertName"].str.contains("credential theft")] </code></pre>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P><span class="lia-media-object lia-media-is-center lia-media-size-large" data-image-alt="PeteBryan_3-1637201699571.png"><button class="lia-media-unstyled-btn" type="button" aria-haspopup="true" aria-label="Enlarge Image PeteBryan_3-1637201699571.png"><img src="https://techcommunity.microsoft.com/t5/s/gxcuf89792/images/bS0yOTc3NzQ1LTMyNzg1Mmk4OThGMDNGQjA5RDg3QUMw?image-dimensions=999x332&amp;revision=14" width="999" height="332" alt="PeteBryan_3-1637201699571.png" /></button><span class="lia-media-caption-text">Searching for rows of a DataFrame matching a criteria</span></span></P>
<P style="border: solid 1px; padding: 10px; background-color: #fafaff;"><STRONG>Tip: </STRONG>Pandas has loads and loads of features to help you find, analyze, transform, and visualize data. As Pandas data structures are key to Microsoft Sentinel Notebooks, we recommended you spend some time getting familiar with some of their features they offer - <A href="https://pandas.pydata.org/" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow noreferrer">https://pandas.pydata.org/</A>&nbsp;</P>

<H2 id="community-2977745-toc-hId--1867983271"><SPAN data-contrast="none">Enriching data using external data sources</SPAN><SPAN data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}">&nbsp;</SPAN></H2>
<P><SPAN data-contrast="auto">One of the powerful elements of&nbsp;Notebooks is&nbsp;combining&nbsp;data from&nbsp;Microsoft Sentinel&nbsp;with data from other sources. One of the most common sources of this data in security is Threat Intelligence (TI) data.&nbsp;MSTICPy&nbsp;has&nbsp;support&nbsp;for&nbsp;several&nbsp;Threat Intelligence data sources including:</SPAN><SPAN data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}">&nbsp;</SPAN></P>
<UL>
<LI data-leveltext="-" data-font="Calibri" data-listid="4" aria-setsize="-1" data-aria-posinset="0" data-aria-level="1"><SPAN data-contrast="auto">VirtusTotal</SPAN><SPAN data-ccp-props="{&quot;134233279&quot;:true,&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}">&nbsp;</SPAN></LI>
<LI data-leveltext="-" data-font="Calibri" data-listid="4" aria-setsize="-1" data-aria-posinset="0" data-aria-level="1"><SPAN data-contrast="auto">GreyNoise</SPAN><SPAN data-ccp-props="{&quot;134233279&quot;:true,&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}">&nbsp;</SPAN></LI>
<LI data-leveltext="-" data-font="Calibri" data-listid="4" aria-setsize="-1" data-aria-posinset="0" data-aria-level="1"><SPAN data-contrast="auto">AlienVault OTX</SPAN><SPAN data-ccp-props="{&quot;134233279&quot;:true,&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}">&nbsp;</SPAN></LI>
<LI data-leveltext="-" data-font="Calibri" data-listid="4" aria-setsize="-1" data-aria-posinset="0" data-aria-level="1"><SPAN data-contrast="auto">IBM&nbsp;XForce</SPAN><SPAN data-ccp-props="{&quot;134233279&quot;:true,&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}">&nbsp;</SPAN></LI>
<LI data-leveltext="-" data-font="Calibri" data-listid="4" aria-setsize="-1" data-aria-posinset="0" data-aria-level="1"><SPAN data-contrast="auto">Microsoft Sentinel&nbsp;TI data</SPAN><SPAN data-ccp-props="{&quot;134233279&quot;:true,&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}">&nbsp;</SPAN></LI>
</UL>
<UL>
<LI data-leveltext="-" data-font="Calibri" data-listid="4" aria-setsize="-1" data-aria-posinset="0" data-aria-level="1"><SPAN data-contrast="auto">OPR (for PageRank details)</SPAN><SPAN data-ccp-props="{&quot;134233279&quot;:true,&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}">&nbsp;</SPAN></LI>
<LI data-leveltext="-" data-font="Calibri" data-listid="4" aria-setsize="-1" data-aria-posinset="0" data-aria-level="1"><SPAN data-contrast="auto">ToR&nbsp;ExitNode&nbsp;information.</SPAN><SPAN data-ccp-props="{&quot;134233279&quot;:true,&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}">&nbsp;</SPAN></LI>
</UL>
<P><SPAN data-contrast="auto">The first step in using these TI sources is to create a `</SPAN><A href="https://msticpy.readthedocs.io/en/latest/data_acquisition/TIProviders.html" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow noreferrer"><SPAN data-contrast="none">TILookup</SPAN></A><SPAN data-contrast="auto">` object.&nbsp;This&nbsp;can then be used to perform lookups against the various supported providers.</SPAN><SPAN data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}">&nbsp;</SPAN></P>
<P><SPAN data-contrast="auto">Lookups can be done against individual items via `.lookup_ioc` or against multiple items with `.lookup_iocs` and you can configure things such as which Threat Intelligence sources are used.</SPAN><SPAN data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}">&nbsp;</SPAN></P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<pre class="lia-code-sample language-python"><code>ti = TILookup()
ti.lookup_iocs(signin_df, obs_col="IPAddress", providers=["GreyNoise"]) </code></pre>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P><span class="lia-media-object lia-media-is-center lia-media-size-large" data-image-alt="PeteBryan_4-1637201760699.png"><button class="lia-media-unstyled-btn" type="button" aria-haspopup="true" aria-label="Enlarge Image PeteBryan_4-1637201760699.png"><img src="https://techcommunity.microsoft.com/t5/s/gxcuf89792/images/bS0yOTc3NzQ1LTMyNzg1M2lGODE3MUI5MzUxRjA4RDU5?image-dimensions=999x400&amp;revision=14" width="999" height="400" alt="PeteBryan_4-1637201760699.png" /></button><span class="lia-media-caption-text">Lookup_iocs results</span></span></P>
<P><SPAN class="TextRun SCXW132078103 BCX8" data-contrast="auto"><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW132078103 BCX8">To make viewing results easier there is a<SPAN>&nbsp;</SPAN></SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW132078103 BCX8">widget to allow you to interactively browse results:</SPAN></SPAN><SPAN class="EOP SCXW132078103 BCX8" data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}">&nbsp;</SPAN></P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<pre class="lia-code-sample language-python"><code>ti.browse_results(ti_df) </code></pre>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P><span class="lia-media-object lia-media-is-center lia-media-size-large" data-image-alt="PeteBryan_5-1637201816779.png"><button class="lia-media-unstyled-btn" type="button" aria-haspopup="true" aria-label="Enlarge Image PeteBryan_5-1637201816779.png"><img src="https://techcommunity.microsoft.com/t5/s/gxcuf89792/images/bS0yOTc3NzQ1LTMyNzg1NGk1QTRCQkE0QUE3NjhGQzg0?image-dimensions=999x864&amp;revision=14" width="999" height="864" alt="PeteBryan_5-1637201816779.png" /></button><span class="lia-media-caption-text">TI results browser widget</span></span></P>
<H3 aria-level="3" id="community-2977745-toc-hId--1177421797"><SPAN data-contrast="none">Azure API&nbsp;Access</SPAN><SPAN data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559738&quot;:40,&quot;335559739&quot;:0,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}">&nbsp;</SPAN></H3>
<P><SPAN data-contrast="auto">MSTICPy&nbsp;also has integration with a range of Azure APIs that can be used to retrieve additional information or perform actions&nbsp;such as get Microsoft Sentinel incidents.</SPAN><SPAN data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}">&nbsp;</SPAN></P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<pre class="lia-code-sample language-python"><code>from msticpy.data.azure_sentinel import AzureSentinel
azs = AzureSentinel()
azs.connect()
azs.get_incident(incident_id = "7c768f11-31f1-46ca-8a5c-25df2e6b7021", sub_id = "8df49d90-99eb-4c31-985d-64b3f33caa93", res_grp= "sent", ws_name="workspace") </code></pre>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P><span class="lia-media-object lia-media-is-center lia-media-size-large" data-image-alt="PeteBryan_6-1637201875147.png"><button class="lia-media-unstyled-btn" type="button" aria-haspopup="true" aria-label="Enlarge Image PeteBryan_6-1637201875147.png"><img src="https://techcommunity.microsoft.com/t5/s/gxcuf89792/images/bS0yOTc3NzQ1LTMyNzg1NWlGRkZDMkYxMjQxOTJEQjcy?image-dimensions=999x358&amp;revision=14" width="999" height="358" alt="PeteBryan_6-1637201875147.png" /></button><span class="lia-media-caption-text">Output of Azure APIs</span></span></P>
<P><SPAN class="TextRun SCXW113191619 BCX8" data-contrast="auto"><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW113191619 BCX8">You can find out more about<SPAN>&nbsp;</SPAN></SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SpellingErrorV2 SCXW113191619 BCX8">MSTICPy’s</SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW113191619 BCX8"><SPAN>&nbsp;</SPAN>support for Azure APIs in the documentation:<SPAN>&nbsp;</SPAN></SPAN></SPAN><A class="Hyperlink SCXW113191619 BCX8" href="https://msticpy.readthedocs.io/en/latest/data_acquisition/AzureData.html" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener nofollow"><SPAN class="TextRun Underlined SCXW113191619 BCX8" data-contrast="none"><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW113191619 BCX8" data-ccp-charstyle="Hyperlink">https://msticpy.readthedocs.io/en/latest/data_acquisition/AzureData.html</SPAN></SPAN></A><SPAN class="TextRun SCXW113191619 BCX8" data-contrast="auto"><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW113191619 BCX8"><SPAN>&nbsp;</SPAN>&amp;<SPAN>&nbsp;</SPAN></SPAN></SPAN><A class="Hyperlink SCXW113191619 BCX8" href="https://msticpy.readthedocs.io/en/latest/data_acquisition/AzureSentinel.html" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener nofollow"><SPAN class="TextRun Underlined SCXW113191619 BCX8" data-contrast="none"><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW113191619 BCX8" data-ccp-charstyle="Hyperlink">https://msticpy.readthedocs.io/en/latest/data_acquisition/AzureSentinel.html</SPAN></SPAN></A><SPAN class="TextRun SCXW113191619 BCX8" data-contrast="auto"><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW113191619 BCX8">&nbsp;</SPAN></SPAN><SPAN class="EOP SCXW113191619 BCX8" data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}">&nbsp;</SPAN></P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<H2 aria-level="2" id="community-2977745-toc-hId-485844838"><SPAN data-contrast="none">Visualizations with&nbsp;MSTICPy&nbsp;&nbsp;</SPAN><SPAN data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559738&quot;:40,&quot;335559739&quot;:0,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}">&nbsp;</SPAN></H2>
<P><SPAN data-contrast="auto">The ability to create complex, interactive visualizations is one of the key benefits of&nbsp;Notebooks, allowing analysts to see data in&nbsp;a unique way&nbsp;and use it to&nbsp;identify&nbsp;patterns of&nbsp;anomalies&nbsp;that may not otherwise be possible to&nbsp;identify.&nbsp;</SPAN><SPAN data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}">&nbsp;</SPAN></P>
<P><SPAN data-contrast="auto">Creating these&nbsp;visualizations&nbsp;from scratch can be quite&nbsp;a&nbsp;complex&nbsp;task&nbsp;and involve a lot of code&nbsp;if&nbsp;starting from nothing.&nbsp;To make the process easier&nbsp;MSTICPy&nbsp;contains&nbsp;several&nbsp;common&nbsp;visualizations&nbsp;work out the box with common data sources from Microsoft Sentinel, and&nbsp;that can quickly and easily be called with minimal code.</SPAN><SPAN data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}">&nbsp;</SPAN></P>
<P><SPAN data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}">&nbsp;</SPAN></P>
<H3 aria-level="3" id="community-2977745-toc-hId--1192526906"><SPAN data-contrast="none">Timelines</SPAN><SPAN data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559738&quot;:40,&quot;335559739&quot;:0,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}">&nbsp;</SPAN></H3>
<P><SPAN data-contrast="auto">Understanding when events occurred and in what order is&nbsp;a key&nbsp;component&nbsp;of many security investigations.&nbsp;MSTICPy&nbsp;can&nbsp;plot&nbsp;diverse types&nbsp;of timelines&nbsp;with&nbsp;several types&nbsp;of data.</SPAN><SPAN data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}">&nbsp;</SPAN></P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<pre class="lia-code-sample language-python"><code>user_df = qry_prov.Azure.list_aad_signins_for_account(account_name="pdemo@seccxpninja.onmicrosoft.com")
timeline.display_timeline(user_df, source_columns=["UserPrincipalName", "ResultType"] </code></pre>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P><span class="lia-media-object lia-media-is-center lia-media-size-large" data-image-alt="PeteBryan_0-1637202590462.png"><button class="lia-media-unstyled-btn" type="button" aria-haspopup="true" aria-label="Enlarge Image PeteBryan_0-1637202590462.png"><img src="https://techcommunity.microsoft.com/t5/s/gxcuf89792/images/bS0yOTc3NzQ1LTMyNzg1N2k4MDVGRDA3NDY4RjUxMkU0?image-dimensions=999x575&amp;revision=14" width="999" height="575" alt="PeteBryan_0-1637202590462.png" /></button><span class="lia-media-caption-text">Timeline visualization</span></span></P>
<P style="border: solid 1px; padding: 10px; background-color: #fafaff;"><STRONG>Troubleshooting Tip: </STRONG> If you are defining columns from a DataFrame as a parameter in another function (as we do above with source_columns) you can sometimes run into issues if you specify a column that does not exist. If you want to see what columns a DataFrame has you can call `DataFrame.columns` to get a list of all the columns.</P>
<P><SPAN class="TextRun SCXW227979487 BCX8" data-contrast="auto"><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW227979487 BCX8">We can also plot time lines showing events with a duration rather than a single time stamp with<SPAN>&nbsp;</SPAN></SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW227979487 BCX8">`</SPAN></SPAN><SPAN class="TextRun SCXW227979487 BCX8" data-contrast="none"><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW227979487 BCX8"><SPAN>&nbsp;</SPAN></SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SpellingErrorV2 SCXW227979487 BCX8">display_timeline_duration</SPAN><SPAN class="NormalTextRun SCXW227979487 BCX8">`:</SPAN></SPAN><SPAN class="EOP SCXW227979487 BCX8" data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:2,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:255}">&nbsp;</SPAN></P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<pre class="lia-code-sample language-python"><code>timeline_duration.display_timeline_duration(alert_df, group_by="AlertName", time_column="StartTimeUtc", end_time_column="EndTimeUtc") </code></pre>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P><span class="lia-media-object lia-media-is-center lia-media-size-large" data-image-alt="PeteBryan_1-1637202649447.png"><button class="lia-media-unstyled-btn" type="button" aria-haspopup="true" aria-label="Enlarge Image PeteBryan_1-1637202649447.png"><img src="https://techcommunity.microsoft.com/t5/s/gxcuf89792/images/bS0yOTc3NzQ1LTMyNzg1OGk3NjYwRjU0QkE2ODIyNURC?image-dimensions=999x505&amp;revision=14" width="999" height="505" alt="PeteBryan_1-1637202649447.png" /></button><span class="lia-media-caption-text">Timeline duration visualization</span></span></P>
<P style="border: solid 1px; padding: 10px; background-color: #fafaff;"><STRONG>Tip: </STRONG> You can also call the timeline visualization directly from a DataFrame with ‘mp_plot’</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<pre class="lia-code-sample language-python"><code>alert_df.mp_plot.timeline(group_by="Severity", source_columns=["AlertName", "TimeGenerated"]) </code></pre>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P><span class="lia-media-object lia-media-is-center lia-media-size-large" data-image-alt="PeteBryan_2-1637202709464.png"><button class="lia-media-unstyled-btn" type="button" aria-haspopup="true" aria-label="Enlarge Image PeteBryan_2-1637202709464.png"><img src="https://techcommunity.microsoft.com/t5/s/gxcuf89792/images/bS0yOTc3NzQ1LTMyNzg1OWlGRUE1MTFGODcwREQ4Rjg1?image-dimensions=999x563&amp;revision=14" width="999" height="563" alt="PeteBryan_2-1637202709464.png" /></button><span class="lia-media-caption-text">Grouped timeline visualization</span></span></P>
<H3 aria-level="3" id="community-2977745-toc-hId-1294985927"><SPAN data-contrast="none">Matrix Plots</SPAN><SPAN data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559738&quot;:40,&quot;335559739&quot;:0,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}">&nbsp;</SPAN></H3>
<P><SPAN data-contrast="auto">The Matrix Plot graph in&nbsp;MSTICPy&nbsp;allows you to plot the interactions between two elements in your data.&nbsp;This can be useful for seeing the relationships between points in a dataset, for example if you wanted to see how often certain IP addresses are&nbsp;communicating&nbsp;with each other&nbsp;in a network you can create a matrix plot with a source IP address on one axis, and a destination IP address on the other axis.</SPAN><SPAN data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}">&nbsp;</SPAN></P>
<P><SPAN data-contrast="auto">As with the timeline plots,&nbsp;the matrix plot can be created directly from a&nbsp;DataFrame&nbsp;using `mp_plot`:</SPAN><SPAN data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}">&nbsp;</SPAN></P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<pre class="lia-code-sample language-python"><code>network_data.mp_plot.matrix(x="SourceIP", y="DestinationIP", title="IP Interaction") </code></pre>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P><span class="lia-media-object lia-media-is-center lia-media-size-large" data-image-alt="PeteBryan_3-1637202744371.png"><button class="lia-media-unstyled-btn" type="button" aria-haspopup="true" aria-label="Enlarge Image PeteBryan_3-1637202744371.png"><img src="https://techcommunity.microsoft.com/t5/s/gxcuf89792/images/bS0yOTc3NzQ1LTMyNzg2MGk1MzM1QTA4OTk1Qjc5RERG?image-dimensions=999x853&amp;revision=14" width="999" height="853" alt="PeteBryan_3-1637202744371.png" /></button><span class="lia-media-caption-text">Matrix visualization</span></span></P>
<H3 aria-level="2" id="community-2977745-toc-hId--512468536"><SPAN data-contrast="none">Widgets</SPAN><SPAN data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559738&quot;:40,&quot;335559739&quot;:0,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}">&nbsp;</SPAN></H3>
<P><SPAN data-contrast="auto">We have seen a couple of widgets already in the query and threat intelligence result browsers. These widgets make&nbsp;Notebooks much more accessible by providing a visual way to&nbsp;interact and&nbsp;customize them without having to write any code.&nbsp;MSTICPy&nbsp;includes a number visual, interactive widgets to allow users to select various parameters to customize the&nbsp;Notebook.</SPAN><SPAN data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}">&nbsp;</SPAN></P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<pre class="lia-code-sample language-python"><code>network_vendor_data_q = "CommonSecurityLog | summarize by DeviceVendor"
network_vendor_data = qry_prov.exec_query(network_vendor_data_q)
network_selector = nbwidgets.SelectItem(
    item_list=network_vendor_data["DeviceVendor"].to_list(),
    description='Select a vendor',
    action=print,
    auto_display=True
); </code></pre>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P><span class="lia-media-object lia-media-is-center lia-media-size-large" data-image-alt="PeteBryan_4-1637202793259.png"><button class="lia-media-unstyled-btn" type="button" aria-haspopup="true" aria-label="Enlarge Image PeteBryan_4-1637202793259.png"><img src="https://techcommunity.microsoft.com/t5/s/gxcuf89792/images/bS0yOTc3NzQ1LTMyNzg2MWkwMzkzRjRCMTgwMzYxRTRF?image-dimensions=999x473&amp;revision=14" width="999" height="473" alt="PeteBryan_4-1637202793259.png" /></button><span class="lia-media-caption-text">Using the SelectItem widget to select a network vendor from data</span></span></P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<pre class="lia-code-sample language-python"><code>q_times = nbwidgets.QueryTime(units='day', max_before=20, before=5, max_after=1)
q_times.display() </code></pre>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>

<P><span class="lia-media-object lia-media-is-center lia-media-size-large" data-image-alt="PeteBryan_5-1637202823185.png"><button class="lia-media-unstyled-btn" type="button" aria-haspopup="true" aria-label="Enlarge Image PeteBryan_5-1637202823185.png"><img src="https://techcommunity.microsoft.com/t5/s/gxcuf89792/images/bS0yOTc3NzQ1LTMyNzg2MmkxMDVEMENBOTY4RjIwMzFE?image-dimensions=999x291&amp;revision=14" width="999" height="291" alt="PeteBryan_5-1637202823185.png" /></button><span class="lia-media-caption-text">Time range selection widget</span></span></P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<P>&nbsp;</P>
<pre class="lia-code-sample language-python"><code>security_alerts = qry_prov.SecurityAlert.list_alerts(add_query_items="| take 10")
alert_select = nbwidgets.SelectAlert(alerts=security_alerts, action=nbdisplay.display_alert)
display(Markdown('### Alert selector with action=DisplayAlert'))
display(HTML("&lt;b&gt; Alert selector with action=DisplayAlert &lt;/b&gt;"))
alert_select.display() </code></pre>

<H2 aria-level="2" id="community-2977745-toc-hId-1845961578"><SPAN data-contrast="none">What to do Next</SPAN><SPAN data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559738&quot;:40,&quot;335559739&quot;:0,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}">&nbsp;</SPAN></H2>
<P><SPAN data-contrast="auto">What you have seen here is just a tiny taster of what Microsoft Sentinel&nbsp;Notebooks can do. However,&nbsp;luckily,&nbsp;we have a lot of additional resources to help you learn&nbsp;what you need and get started with&nbsp;Notebooks.</SPAN><SPAN data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}">&nbsp;</SPAN></P>
<P><SPAN data-contrast="auto">We recommend that you do the following:</SPAN><SPAN data-ccp-props="{&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}">&nbsp;</SPAN></P>
<UL>
<LI><SPAN data-contrast="auto">Sign up&nbsp;for&nbsp;the&nbsp;webinar&nbsp;below&nbsp;where we will cover&nbsp;the&nbsp;topics in this blog in an interactive manner,&nbsp;where you can see the code being executed and learn some extra hints and tips about running&nbsp;Notebooks.&nbsp;</SPAN><SPAN data-ccp-props="{&quot;134233279&quot;:true,&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}">&nbsp;</SPAN></LI>
<LI><SPAN data-contrast="auto">December 16</SPAN><SPAN data-contrast="auto">th</SPAN><SPAN data-contrast="auto">&nbsp;2021&nbsp;- Become&nbsp;a&nbsp;Jupyter&nbsp;Notebooks Ninja –&nbsp;MSTICPy&nbsp;Fundamentals to Build Your Own&nbsp;Notebooks&nbsp;-&nbsp;</SPAN><A href="https://forms.office.com/pages/responsepage.aspx?id=v4j5cvGGr0GRqy180BHbR2HneBfpDd1Mj3-yGKE5Q-xUNkVRQkNPTlFXSzVFRzZFSURFWkRKM0hWUi4u" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer"><SPAN data-contrast="none">Sign Up Here</SPAN></A><SPAN data-ccp-props="{&quot;134233279&quot;:true,&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}">&nbsp;</SPAN></LI>
<LI><SPAN data-contrast="auto">Run the Getting Started&nbsp;Notebook&nbsp;in&nbsp;Microsoft Sentinel</SPAN><SPAN data-ccp-props="{&quot;134233279&quot;:true,&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}">&nbsp;</SPAN>
<UL>
<LI><SPAN data-contrast="auto">This will help you get your config set up</SPAN><SPAN data-ccp-props="{&quot;134233279&quot;:true,&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}">&nbsp;</SPAN></LI>
<LI><SPAN data-contrast="auto">This&nbsp;</SPAN><A href="https://docs.microsoft.com/en-us/azure/sentinel/notebook-get-started" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer"><SPAN>Documentation</SPAN></A><SPAN data-contrast="auto">&nbsp;will help you in running this notebook&nbsp;</SPAN><SPAN data-ccp-props="{&quot;134233279&quot;:true,&quot;201341983&quot;:0,&quot;335559739&quot;:160,&quot;335559740&quot;:259}">&nbsp;</SPAN></LI>

</UL>

aria-level=\"2\" id=\"community-2977745-toc-hId--293249455\"\u003e\u003cSPAN data-contrast=\"none\"\u003eInstalling and Importing Packages in Python\u003c/SPAN\u003e\u003cSPAN data-ccp-props=\"{\u0026quot;201341983\u0026quot;:0,\u0026quot;335559738\u0026quot;:40,\u0026quot;335559739\u0026quot;:0,\u0026quot;335559740\u0026quot;:259}\"\u003e\u0026nbsp;\u003c/SPAN\u003e\u003c/H2\u003e\n\u003cP\u003e\u003cSPAN data-contrast=\"auto\"\u003eOne of the\u0026nbsp;important things\u0026nbsp;about using Python in\u0026nbsp;Notebooks is that you can install and use code libraries (referred to as packages) created by others, allowing you to access the functionality they provide without having to code them yourself.\u003c/SPAN\u003e\u003cSPAN data-ccp-props=\"{\u0026quot;201341983\u0026quot;:0,\u0026quot;335559739\u0026quot;:160,\u0026quot;335559740\u0026quot;:259}\"\u003e\u0026nbsp;\u003c/SPAN\u003e\u003c/P\u003e\n\u003cP\u003e\u003cSPAN data-contrast=\"auto\"\u003eThere are several ways to install\u0026nbsp;Python packages\u0026nbsp;depending on how you want to\u0026nbsp;find and\u0026nbsp;access the\u0026nbsp;packages, however the simplest and easiest is using pip. Pip\u0026nbsp;(\u003cA href=\"https://pypi.org/project/pip/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener nofollow noreferrer\"\u003ehttps://pypi.org/project/pip/\u003c/A\u003e) is the\u0026nbsp;package\u0026nbsp;installer for Python and makes finding and installing Python\u0026nbsp;packages\u0026nbsp;simple.\u003c/SPAN\u003e\u003cSPAN data-ccp-props=\"{\u0026quot;201341983\u0026quot;:0,\u0026quot;335559739\u0026quot;:160,\u0026quot;335559740\u0026quot;:259}\"\u003e\u0026nbsp;\u003c/SPAN\u003e\u003c/P\u003e\n\u003cP\u003e\u003cSPAN data-contrast=\"auto\"\u003eYou can use pip to install packages via the command line, or if you are using a\u0026nbsp;Notebook, directly in a\u0026nbsp;Notebook\u0026nbsp;cell.\u0026nbsp;Installing directly in a\u0026nbsp;Notebook\u0026nbsp;is often preferred as it ensures that you are installing the package in the same Python environment the\u0026nbsp;Notebook\u0026nbsp;is being executed in.\u0026nbsp;To\u0026nbsp;install via a\u0026nbsp;Notebook\u0026nbsp;code\u0026nbsp;cell,\u0026nbsp;we\u0026nbsp;need to use `%pip` followed by install and the\u0026nbsp;package\u0026nbsp;name. e.g.:\u003c/SPAN\u003e\u003cSPAN data-ccp-props=\"{\u0026quot;201341983\u0026quot;:0,\u0026quot;335559739\u0026quot;:160,\u0026quot;335559740\u0026quot;:259}\"\u003e\u0026nbsp;\u003c/SPAN\u003e\u003c/P\u003e\n\u003cP\u003e\u0026nbsp;\u003c/P\u003e\n\u003cP\u003e\u0026nbsp;\u003c/P\u003e\n\u003cP\u003e\u0026nbsp;\u003c/P\u003e\n\u003cP\u003e\u0026nbsp;\u003c/P\u003e\n\u003cP\u003e\u0026nbsp;\u003c/P\u003e\n\u003cpre class=\"lia-code-sample language-python\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003e%pip install requests\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\n\u003cP\u003e\u0026nbsp;\u003c/P\u003e\n\u003cP\u003e\u0026nbsp;\u003c/P\u003e\n\u003cP\u003e\u0026nbsp;\u003c/P\u003e\n\u003cP\u003e\u0026nbsp;\u003c/P\u003e\n\u003cP\u003e\u0026nbsp;\u003c/P\u003e\n\u003cP\u003e\u003cspan alt=\"PeteBryan_0-1637179707416.png\" /\u003e\u003c/button\u003e\u003cspan class=\"lia-media-caption-text\"\u003eNotebook output of running %pip install
